1924: The Silent Decade

by ItsAstronomical

with the help of MassachusettsForStockdale, Lurker, River, and Gelid Lagopus

Congrats on finding the secret route! Obviously, this is non-canon.

Sources

Calvin Coolidge, the GOP, and Teapot Dome

Calvin Coolidge is nothing short of an American Engima.
Despite my issues with him, he has often been misinterpreted by modern conservative commentators.
I hope this mod provides a better overview of his early administration and character.
We also ought to consider the party he served under and his predecessor's scandals he had to overcome.

Robert Sobel - Coolidge: An American Enigma
Amity Shlaes - Coolidge
William Edward Leuchtenburg - The Perils of Prosperity, 1914-32
J. Leonard Bates - The Teapot Dome Scandal and the Election of 1924
Robert James Maddox - Keeping Cool with Coolidge

John Davis and the Democratic Party

John Davis was a dark horse and a compromise candidate forced to be the sacrificial lamb for that year.
Nevertheless, he arguably represented the last breaths of an older type of Democrat.
To understand Davis and his position in 1924 is to understand the Democratic party at that point.
William Gibbs McAdoo was arguably the frontrunner for the nomination for awhile.
Therefore, research was done into how his campaign handled the convention.

Robert K. Murray - The 103rd Ballot
William Henry Harbaugh - Lawyer's lawyer; the life of John W. Davis
Philip M Chase - William Gibbs McAdoo: The last Progressive, (1863–1941)

Robert La Follette and the Progressive Movement

1924 was La Follette's last stand. He died the next year.
Therefore, this campaign is considered a sort of 'best hits' of his lifetime.
I included his autobiography here, of course with other sources as well.

Robert La Follette - La Follette's Autobiography; a personal narrative of political experiences
Richard Drake - The Education of an Anti-Imperialist: Robert La Follette and U.S. Expansion
Scott D. Johnston - Robert LaFollette and the Socialists

Sean Munger's YouTube Video

During my early work on this mod, I frequently received messages from people giving this 2-hour YouTube video as a source for the mod.
While getting all the twist-and-turns with CYOA required more information than one video can provide, I still recommend this video!
I also do wanna thank everyone who sent me this. Your support is nice and it helps.


Sean Munger - 1924: The Fascinating Forgotten Election

Special Thanks

This one took awhile, but I wanna thank all the playtesters. I appreciate it a bunch.
Mango helped with a couple coding things.
Lurker helped make a lot of outlines which made the writing process easier for me.
Thank you to Luuwuu for everything, obviously.
Oh, and of course...

...thank you for playing!

1924: The Silent Decade

by ItsAstronomical

with the help of MassachusettsForStockdale, Lurker, River, and Gelid Lagopus

Sources

Calvin Coolidge, the GOP, and Teapot Dome

Calvin Coolidge is nothing short of an American Engima.
Despite my issues with him, he has often been misinterpreted by modern conservative commentators.
I hope this mod provides a better overview of his early administration and character.
We also ought to consider the party he served under and his predecessor's scandals he had to overcome.

Robert Sobel - Coolidge: An American Enigma
Amity Shlaes - Coolidge
William Edward Leuchtenburg - The Perils of Prosperity, 1914-32
J. Leonard Bates - The Teapot Dome Scandal and the Election of 1924
Robert James Maddox - Keeping Cool with Coolidge

John Davis and the Democratic Party

John Davis was a dark horse and a compromise candidate forced to be the sacrificial lamb for that year.
Nevertheless, he arguably represented the last breaths of an older type of Democrat.
To understand Davis and his position in 1924 is to understand the Democratic party at that point.
William Gibbs McAdoo was arguably the frontrunner for the nomination for awhile.
Therefore, research was done into how his campaign handled the convention.

Robert K. Murray - The 103rd Ballot
William Henry Harbaugh - Lawyer's lawyer; the life of John W. Davis
Philip M Chase - William Gibbs McAdoo: The last Progressive, (1863–1941)

Robert La Follette and the Progressive Movement

1924 was La Follette's last stand. He died the next year.
Therefore, this campaign is considered a sort of 'best hits' of his lifetime.
I included his autobiography here, of course with other sources as well.

Robert La Follette - La Follette's Autobiography; a personal narrative of political experiences
Richard Drake - The Education of an Anti-Imperialist: Robert La Follette and U.S. Expansion
Scott D. Johnston - Robert LaFollette and the Socialists

Sean Munger's YouTube Video

During my early work on this mod, I frequently received messages from people giving this 2-hour YouTube video as a source for the mod.
While getting all the twist-and-turns with CYOA required more information than one video can provide, I still recommend this video!
I also do wanna thank everyone who sent me this. Your support is nice and it helps.

Therefore, research was done into how his campaign handled the convention.

Robert K. Murray - The 103rd Ballot
William Henry Harbaugh - Lawyer's lawyer; the life of John W. Davis
Philip M Chase - William Gibbs McAdoo: The last Progressive, (1863–1941)

Robert La Follette and the Progressive Movement

1924 was La Follette's last stand. He died the next year.
Therefore, this campaign is considered a sort of 'best hits' of his lifetime.
I included his autobiography here, of course with other sources as well.

Robert La Follette - La Follette's Autobiography; a personal narrative of political experiences
Richard Drake - The Education of an Anti-Imperialist: Robert La Follette and U.S. Expansion
Scott D. Johnston - Robert LaFollette and the Socialists

Sean Munger's YouTube Video

During my early work on this mod, I frequently received messages from people giving this 2-hour YouTube video as a source for the mod.
While getting all the twist-and-turns with CYOA required more information than one video can provide, I still recommend this video!
I also do wanna thank everyone who sent me this. Your support is nice and it helps.


Sean Munger - 1924: The Fascinating Forgotten Election

Why did Coolidge personally attend Thomas Marshall's funeral?- posted on /r/AskHistorians

I was told that back in the day, it was quite uncommon for sitting Presidents to attend funerals, and would instead send their Vice President or a member of cabient to represent them. The first major example of this was Coolidge going to former VP Marshall (and his opponent in 1924)'s funeral.

Why is that though? My understanding was that the campaign was rough and aggressive on both sides. Would Coolidge not be mad that Marshall almost costed him the White House?

u/Awesome-Hyena-524- +4
Perhaps. But Coolidge was not a man to hold grudges, and Mr. Marshall did seem to get along okay with Coolidge in their limited interactions. After the 1920 campaign, Marshall sent a witty telegram to Coolidge, offering “sincere condolences” for his misfortune in being elected vice president.

What Marshall and Coolidge both had in common is they were, at one point, Vice Presidents. The struggle of this role can be explained with another one of Marshall's joke - "A woman had two sons. One son went to sea. The other was elected vice president. Neither was ever heard of again."

Indiana Klan | From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

The Indiana Klan was the state of Indiana branch of the Ku Klux Klan, a secret society in the United States that organized in 1915 to promote ideas of racial superiority and affect public affairs on issues of Prohibition, education, political corruption, and morality. Like the rest of the KKK, it was strongly white supremacist against African Americans, Chinese Americans, and also Catholics and Jews, whose faiths were commonly associated with Irish, Italian, Balkan, and Slavic immigrants and their descendants

The Indiana Klan rose to prominence beginning in the early 1920s after World War I, when white Protestants felt threatened by social and political issues, including changes caused by decades of immigration from southern and eastern Europe. Indiana's Klan was one of the strongest in the country, with a large percentage of the entire White Protestant male population being members.

.......

Peak of Influence and Downfall

At the height of its power, the Klan had over 250,000 members. The highest concentration was in cities in the central part of the state. Klan membership was discouraged in some parts of the state; in New Albany, for instance, city leaders denounced the Klan and discouraged residents from joining. Other cities, including Indianapolis, were almost completely controlled by the Klan, and election to public office was impossible without their support.

However - the nomination of Indiana Senator Samuel Ralston by the Democratic Party in the 1924 Presidential Election ironically helped contribute to the organization's downfall. While Ralston never made any public declarations in support of the Klan, his ties lingered on the national stage as he campaigned. When the election became deadlocked - the first time since 1824, these ties made many reluctant to allow him to come to power, and thus, Coolidge was easily re-elected in the ensuing contingent election.

UNITED STATES v. COX ENTERPRISES, INC. (1934) - Oyez

Facts of the case

Cox Enterprises had become a large and very profitable company, run by two-time Presidential candidate James Middleton Cox. After a series of acquisitions, including Columbia Broadcasting System, the company, with its large influence over the radio and newspaper industry, sought to reach an agreement amongst fellow radio companies to collectively raise the rates of radio advertisements. The Justice Department sued, arguing that the agreement was price-fixing by Cox Enterprises and other companies.

Question

Under the Sherman Antitrust Act, is a price-fixing agreement illegal per-se?

Conclusion

The Court held, on a 5-4 decision, that the supposed agreement laid out by Cox Enterprises was not illegal. The Court argued that because advertisements were not necessarily an industry, the price of advertisement placements could not necessarily be treated as an activity of commerce. Additionally, the Court reasoned that because advertisements were seen as necessary for radio survival, that the market would eventually return any prices back to their intended level.

' }, }; // Used for when the nominee is finalized function lockInNominee(selectedId) { for (const id in nominees) { nominees[id].isActive = (id === selectedId); } } function addHeadquarterButton() { // Check if the button already exists if (document.getElementById('headquarter_button')) { return; // Insert the new button next to the reference button refButton.insertAdjacentElement('afterend', newButton); } function openHeadquarter() { if (gop >= 4) { gopText = 'at its peak - and the party is in your hands.' } if (gop >= 2 && gop < 4) { gopText = 'increasing, day by day' } if (gop < 2) { gopText = 'minimal and pathetic' } if (equality >= 7) { equalityText = 'one of the most esteemed in history' } if (equality >= 4 && equality < 7) { equalityText = 'uniquely and shockingly strong' } if (equality >= -5 && equality < 4) { equalityText = 'unfortunately weak' } if (equality < -5) { equalityText = 'one of utter shame and disgrace' } if (econ >= 5) { econText = 'very, very conservative' } if (econ >= 0 && econ < 5) { econText = 'somewhat conservative' } if (econ < 0) { econText = 'unorthodox and unpopular with business' } if (prog >= 4) { progText = 'stronger than expected' } if (prog < 4) { progText = 'weak and untrustworthy' } if (corruption >= 2) { corruptionText = 'has seemingly been cleared up and gone away.' } if (corruption < 2) { corruptionText = 'currently lingers and rots the White House' } cabinet += 1;
